  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6560495662238606123">Sixteen-year-old Maya is just an ordinary teen in an ordinary town. Sure, she doesn't know much about her background - the only thing she really has to cling to is an odd paw-print birthmark on her hip - but she never really put much thought into who her parents were or how she ended up with her adopted parents in this tiny medical-research community on Vancouver Island.<br/><br/><i>Un</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6560495662238606123" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old Maya is just an ordinary teen in an ordinary town. Sure, she doesn't know much about her background - the only thing she really has to cling to is an odd paw-print birthmark on her hip - but she never really put much thought into who her parents were or how she ended up with her adopted parents in this tiny medical-research community on Vancouver Island.<br /><br /><i>Until now</i>.<br /><br />Strange things have been happening in this claustrophobic town - from the mountain lions that have been approaching Maya to her best friend's hidden talent for "feeling" out people and situations, to the sexy new bad boy who makes Maya feel...<i>different</i>. Combine that with a few unexplained deaths and a mystery involving Maya's biological parents and it's easy to suspect that this town might have more than its share of skeletons in its closet.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No, you don't have to read the darkest powers before, but if I was you I would. The book will stil make sense, but the series do interlock and in the <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No, you don't have to read the darkest powers before, but if I was you I would. The book will stil make sense, but the series do interlock and in the 3th book the caracters from the darkest powers meet the ones from this series... Also The Darkest Powers Trilogy is awesome!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_95210012" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95210012" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95210012?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95210012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16951438815466813778">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/03/the-gathering-by-kelley-armstrong.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>What a pleasant surprise this novel was! I did not expect to like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896345.The_Gathering__Darkness_Rising___1_' title='The Gathering (Darkness Rising, #1) by Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Gathering</a> after being very underwhelmed by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7581.Kelley_Armstrong' title='Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kelley Armstrong</a>'s first YA trilogy - <i>Darkest Powers</i>. <br/><br/>While I think nothing changed in terms of the structure Armstrong chose for her trilogies (the whole story is simply separated into three parts instead of presenting three separate story arcs), this book was a much better experience for me. I attribute this to the following:<br/><br/>1) Setting - loved, loved that </span>
  <span id="freeText16951438815466813778" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/03/the-gathering-by-kelley-armstrong.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />What a pleasant surprise this novel was! I did not expect to like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896345.The_Gathering__Darkness_Rising___1_" title="The Gathering (Darkness Rising, #1) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering</a> after being very underwhelmed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7581.Kelley_Armstrong" title="Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelley Armstrong</a>'s first YA trilogy - <i>Darkest Powers</i>. <br /><br />While I think nothing changed in terms of the structure Armstrong chose for her trilogies (the whole story is simply separated into three parts instead of presenting three separate story arcs), this book was a much better experience for me. I attribute this to the following:<br /><br />1) Setting - loved, loved that the book is set in Canada, in an isolated tiny medical research town (population: 200) located in a national park. A huge portion of the story takes place outdoors. It made me want to live in a cabin with bobcats and cougars roaming around too. <br /><br />2) New type of supernatural beings - Maya is something Armstrong has never written before. I am quite curious about Maya's powers which are not very clear at the moment. I surely prefer them to Chloe's dead-raising skills.<br /><br />3) No hiding in warehouses! Was very sick of them in all three <i>Darkest Powers</i> books.<br /><br />4) Teen characters and romances - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7581.Kelley_Armstrong" title="Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelley Armstrong</a> is one of a very few YA authors who refuse to promote stalker/doormat relationships based on ANGST. The narrator of this novel - Maya - is a strong young woman and her relationship with her hot love interest is well-balanced, even when complicated.<br /><br />The biggest flaw of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896345.The_Gathering__Darkness_Rising___1_" title="The Gathering (Darkness Rising, #1) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering</a> comes from the author's choice of the trilogy's plot structure. Again, like in <i>Darkest Powers</i>, there is almost no climax in the story, just some mildly exciting action sequence in the last 50 pages or so. Based on the reviews I have read, this flaw can really spoil the experience for some readers.<br /><br />I, however, managed to enjoy the novel anyway. It left me with the same feeling <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> did. I know there are more questions raised than answered, I know it is a very incomplete story and the whole novel does nothing much besides setting up the stage for the future installments, but the process of reading the book was so enjoyable that I was able to overlook its shortcomings and now am looking forward to the sequel with anticipation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16951438815466813778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158095217?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158095217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12260325635506175982"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I have a confession to make... here goes. So, anyone who knows me at all on goodreads will know that I have a few friends whose reviews I rely on without question. If they say a book is better than chocolate, orgasms and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta' title='Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melina Marchetta</a> combined, even if I've never heard of it, I will believe them. Except... I didn't. I doubted, it's true, I doubted. I have had this book on my shelf since not long after it's release in April last year and I have been putting if off and putting it off. Every</span>
  <span id="freeText12260325635506175982" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I have a confession to make... here goes. So, anyone who knows me at all on goodreads will know that I have a few friends whose reviews I rely on without question. If they say a book is better than chocolate, orgasms and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> combined, even if I've never heard of it, I will believe them. Except... I didn't. I doubted, it's true, I doubted. I have had this book on my shelf since not long after it's release in April last year and I have been putting if off and putting it off. Everytime I reminded myself that I should probably read it soon I would then talk myself out of it.<br><br>Why? Because while my love for dystopias keeps me reading trash in search of that one book that will prove authors still know how to do it well, my love for young adult paranormal novels up and left shortly after the publication of the Twilight series. Okay, so it occasionally makes a rare re-appearance for books that are paranormal with other elements, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a> for example. And yet, Ms Armstrong has somehow successfuly delivered it back to me in a shiny, completely addicted condition. I thought my inability to enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> - another book that all my friends' loved - was proof that I was doomed to dislike young adult paranormal books forever. How wrong I was.<br><br>This is a wonderfully enjoyable novel with refreshing Native Canadian mythology. There's also an array of characters that interested me beyond the main character (Maya) and the guy she's hot for (Rafe)... like Daniel - her overprotective best friend, Rafe's mentally-damaged sister - Annie, Sam - the quick-tempered girl who is more than you first expect... even Maya's parents are memorable with all the funny dialogue between the family, especially between Maya and her father. And I want to hug <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7581.Kelley_Armstrong" title="Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelley Armstrong</a> so much for managing to create a sexy love interest without him being a broody, crazy control-freak. A love story where both the guy and the girl have personalities and aren't abusive? I must be dreaming!<br><br>This is just so much better written than the majority of young adult paranormal novels. I'm not suggesting that it will blow your mind or give you a new perspective on life, but this is how I felt about YA UF back when they used to be fun and not so repetitive, cliched and annoying. This is how I felt at the start of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/345627.Vampire_Academy__Vampire_Academy___1_" title="Vampire Academy (Vampire Academy, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a> series: excited.<br></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1608996371" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/10517119-pang">Pang</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=overrated-books">overrated-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608996371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12731220145591672453"><br/>I do not read a lot of paranormal fantasy novels because (forgive me for being too honest), I find most of them a bit corny and the romance often cheesy but this particular book combines several elements-the setting (a really small secluded forest town in Canada that specializes in medical research), the sprinkle of science fiction and mythology and the genuine teen feel to the novel including the realistic romance, dialogues and writing making this a very refreshing read. <br/><br/>The plot isn’t your co</span>
  <span id="freeText12731220145591672453" style="display:none"><br />I do not read a lot of paranormal fantasy novels because (forgive me for being too honest), I find most of them a bit corny and the romance often cheesy but this particular book combines several elements-the setting (a really small secluded forest town in Canada that specializes in medical research), the sprinkle of science fiction and mythology and the genuine teen feel to the novel including the realistic romance, dialogues and writing making this a very refreshing read. <br /><br />The plot isn’t your complex, adventurous type but it was still engaging to read because of the mystery behind the characters, and the setting of the story itself. I learned quite a few things about wild animals especially cougars. ;) The main character, Maya, is also a very likable character, quite funny too. What I particularly liked most about the story is Maya’s relationship with her parents and her best friend, Daniel. Here’s a great example of the plausibility of a boy and a girl being best friends without having to fall in love with each other (although it might be too early to tell because it’s only the first book). But Rafe is &lt;3. <br /><br />I settled for three stars because besides the cliffhanger, the last twenty percent of the story seemed a bit jumbled up, as if the missing actions during the significant first portion of the novel were all crammed up in the last few pages of the book. Also, there are still so many questions unanswered although I’m sure that’s the author’s way of making the reader want to read the sequels. Overall, it was still a generally enjoyable read. :) <br /><br />If you're looking for a really enthusiastic and more positive perspective of the novel, do check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356579277?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Pang's review.</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12731220145591672453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1720908671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720908671" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720908671?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061797033" href="/book/show/11765916-the-gathering">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=got-in-2017">got-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=mad-scientists">mad-scientists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=small-town">small-town</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=magic-powers">magic-powers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720908671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8750879762439347959"><b>"The cougar-a ragged-ear old top I clled Marv-just stared at her, like he couldn't believe anyone would be dumb to climb a tree to escape a cat.” </b><br/><br/>I love Kelley Armstrong’s Women of the Otherworld series, but this was my first time trying one of her young adult series. Her writing style worked fine for this genre, easy to focus on and a breeze to get through. <br/><br/>Not much happens until after 50% into the story, but it’s still easy to stay focused on the character-focused book. The small town setting </span>
  <span id="freeText8750879762439347959" style="display:none"><b>"The cougar-a ragged-ear old top I clled Marv-just stared at her, like he couldn't believe anyone would be dumb to climb a tree to escape a cat.” </b><br /><br />I love Kelley Armstrong’s Women of the Otherworld series, but this was my first time trying one of her young adult series. Her writing style worked fine for this genre, easy to focus on and a breeze to get through. <br /><br />Not much happens until after 50% into the story, but it’s still easy to stay focused on the character-focused book. The small town setting is almost a character in itself, and there are different animals that throw out hints about the main character’s hidden abilities. Set in Canada, the tiny town is a called a medical community of sorts, which is just odd but totally works. Maya’s father is the park ranger so animals and the surrounding woods have much to do with the story. There’s a few scenes in the high school and friend gatherings that keep reminding me this is YA – which isn’t a bad thing since there’s something about school settings that still interests me with stories. <br /><br />Most of the action is reserved for the last 20%, so some may lose some patience. There is a cliffhanger, but thankfully it’s not a jagged killer of one. While not action filled, it stills stays interesting but not much actually happens – the book seems to be one long set-up until the ending where it sorts of abruptly cuts off during their next step.<br /><br />Maya is unique with her abilities and I’m not sure exactly everything she can do – but she explores some of her heritage and Native American origins in this one. I have a feeling she’s going to discover much more in the second book about tribes and her missing people. I don’t know all she can do yet but it’s clearly something with animals.<br /><br />There is romance but it’s not overly angsty. It’s tied strongly into the storyline, of course, but the main love interest is likable and different enough to keep that okay. Her side friend with the abusive fathers throws in more realism. I can’t complain about any of the characters – we have some stereotypes, but in real life the teenagers usually have stereotypes in their group anyway – we don’t develop cliques in high school without a reason…<br /><br />I like Maya’s bond with her adoptive parents and how well they understand her – not something often used in YA fiction – but I’m confused on the end and who or what are her birth parents. Again, have a feeling that information is left to discover in the sequel.<br /><br />A lot of questions are raised and answered, but still some questions dangle waiting for the sequel to come out and fill the reader in. Will be the second when I get the chance.<br /><br />I haven’t read the Darkest Powers trilogy, so this is pretty new to me since I am not familiar with that tie-in series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8750879762439347959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5419899363181653747">The Gathering (Darkness Rising #1), Kelley Armstrong<br/><br/>The Gathering is the first book in Armstrong's Darkness Rising trilogy. Darkness Rising is the second trilogy in the Darkest Powers series. Darkness Rising follows a new set of kids. The Darkness Rising trilogy follows a sixteen-year-old girl named Maya Delaney.<br/><br/>The setting for The Gathering is a small medical-research town called Salmon Creek on Vancouver Island.   <span id="freeText5419899363181653747" style="display:none">The Gathering (Darkness Rising #1), Kelley Armstrong<br /><br />The Gathering is the first book in Armstrong's Darkness Rising trilogy. Darkness Rising is the second trilogy in the Darkest Powers series. Darkness Rising follows a new set of kids. The Darkness Rising trilogy follows a sixteen-year-old girl named Maya Delaney.<br /><br />The setting for The Gathering is a small medical-research town called Salmon Creek on Vancouver Island. Salmon Creek was built by St. Cloud Corporation, the owners of the town and surrounding park. It was built for their employees. Maya, the main character, is the adopted daughter of the park ranger. The events actually start a year before with the death of Maya's friend, Serena. She and Maya were swimming in a lake. Serena, captain of Salmon Creek High swim team, drowned in the lake, and Maya is guilt-ridden for not being able to save her friend.<br /><br />A year later, Maya is getting ready to celebrate her sweet 16. She wants to tattoo her birthmark—a paw-print shape on her hip. She doesn't want it altered in any way, though; she just wants to make it more noticeable. However, she doesn't get it because the tattoo artist's aunt insults her by calling her a witch in Navajo. Later, she invites Rafe, a new bad-boy at school, to her birthday party at Daniel's house. At the party, the teens have a competition on Maya's new rock wall: if she can beat all the guys, they have to add more footholds, but if she loses to even one guy, she has to kiss him.<br /><br />After she defeats all the contestants, Rafe shows up. He challenges Maya individually, and beats her. He doesn't kiss her, though, promising to claim his prize without prying eyes. Maya and Rafe then start going out. One day, when Maya was going over to his house for dinner with him and his childish older sister, Annie, she is attacked by someone looking for Rafe. She sees Annie transform from a cougar into herself. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز دهم ماه فوریه سال 2014 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: دور همی: سری طلوع تاریکی یک؛ نویسنده: کلی آرمسترانگ؛<br /><br />ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_95667233" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95667233" />
    <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship"><img alt="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297107033p2/2109885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95667233?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship">Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781907410178" href="/book/show/7989500-the-gathering">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=dtb">dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=weres-shifters">weres-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95667233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3976078798492385425">Well written but I think my sheer impatience with the set-up got to me. <br/>References to Samuel Lyle (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2800905.The_Summoning__Darkest_Powers___1_' title='The Summoning (Darkest Powers, #1) by Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkest Powers trilogy</a>) and the Nasts, Cortezes and St Clouds (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11918.Bitten__Women_of_the_Otherworld___1_' title='Bitten (Women of the Otherworld, #1) by Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>Women of the Otherworld</a>) were very welcome as I'm anxious to see characters from all the books connect but I'm seeing similarities with these other works too. <br/><br/>Maya reminds me of Elena (WotO) in personality and ability but the people around her made me think of Chloe's crowd. Daniel is <s>Chloe's</s> Maya's best friend and she wants to keep it </span>
  <span id="freeText3976078798492385425" style="display:none">Well written but I think my sheer impatience with the set-up got to me. <br />References to Samuel Lyle (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2800905.The_Summoning__Darkest_Powers___1_" title="The Summoning (Darkest Powers, #1) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkest Powers trilogy</a>) and the Nasts, Cortezes and St Clouds (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11918.Bitten__Women_of_the_Otherworld___1_" title="Bitten (Women of the Otherworld, #1) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Women of the Otherworld</a>) were very welcome as I'm anxious to see characters from all the books connect but I'm seeing similarities with these other works too. <br /><br />Maya reminds me of Elena (WotO) in personality and ability but the people around her made me think of Chloe's crowd. Daniel is <s>Chloe's</s> Maya's best friend and she wants to keep it that way so no kissy-wissy despite being attractive to every girl except her. Apparently. I'm not so sure. And Rafe is her Derek (though he may actually be Clay to her Elena), an outsider/outcast who's struggling to care for his <s>brother</s> sister, Annie.<br /><br />I loved Maya's parents. They were good people and genuinely loved and cared for their adopted daughter. Parents are rarely seen or heard in YA these days or if they're around they're neglectful of their duties, clueless about their children and their actions. Maya has close relationships with them and I chuckled every time she (lovingly) teased her father mercilessly. Her directness was embarrassing!<br /><br />My impatience came into play when everything is blatantly obvious to us readers but we're waiting for the characters to catch on or impart important information to these poor clueless kids. They don't realise that what they're joking around about is actually real and true because to them it's too far-fetched. I feel like I'm 100 steps ahead of them and my foot's itching to kick them to motivate them to catch up.<br /><br />Intellectually I know this is just a slow build up, establishing Maya's world so we can understand how devastating it'll be for her and her friends when it all falls apart but just...HURRY UP! That cliffhanger, I knew it was coming but it still burns. If I had the next instalment I would be reading it right now instead of writing this so I enjoyed the book well enough.<br /><br />However, I didn't particularly take to Rafe. Perhaps I was reading too much into the whole love triangle thing of the last trilogy but I was hoping Daniel would take Maya's dad's offer of the truck and marry Maya. He's far more likeable than Rafe and I got the impression he might be interested in dating Maya but as I said before, I might be reading too much into his actions.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I have many questions about what will happen next. How many of the kids were taken, if any? Did Annie make it out and will we see her again? How is everything going to explained? Who will get what explanation? It's going to be tough to come up with a cover story about the way the fire spread and the strange people with guns pretending to be rescue workers but I think it will be entertaining to see "them" try. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />On a sidenote: the tactile quality of my UK edition is very high. Smooth, soft cover, paper and page edges. Definitely not a cheap mass market paperback.<br /><br />_________________________________________________<br /><br /><br /><i>First 90 pages now available here:</i><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://browseinside.harperteen.com/index.aspx?isbn13=9780061797026">http://browseinside.harperteen.com/in...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3976078798492385425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_125833237" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125833237" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125833237?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=are-we-there-yet">are-we-there-yet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=plot-what-plot">plot-what-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=big-heap-of-meh">big-heap-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=editor-wanted">editor-wanted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=so-boring-it-s-boring">so-boring-it-s-boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=2016-owned-challenge">2016-owned-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=romance-in-disguise">romance-in-disguise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=idiot-protagonist">idiot-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125833237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6561810041278065874">Bullet Review:<br/><br/>75 pages of plot ballooned out to 359 pages. Characters are complete morons, without a shred of common sense. All the plot twists I called A HUNDRED PAGES before the characters were told it (because investigating? Ain't nobody got time for that!). Instead, let's focus on the stupid teen DWAMA romantic plot tumor.<br/><br/>You cannot say that I'm bloating the rating just because I liked Armstrong's earlier books. Massive disappointment; if I didn't already own the rest of the trilogy, I would</span>
  <span id="freeText6561810041278065874" style="display:none">Bullet Review:<br /><br />75 pages of plot ballooned out to 359 pages. Characters are complete morons, without a shred of common sense. All the plot twists I called A HUNDRED PAGES before the characters were told it (because investigating? Ain't nobody got time for that!). Instead, let's focus on the stupid teen DWAMA romantic plot tumor.<br /><br />You cannot say that I'm bloating the rating just because I liked Armstrong's earlier books. Massive disappointment; if I didn't already own the rest of the trilogy, I would quit here.<br /><br />Full Review:<br /><br />Maya is totally not a normal teen in a totally not normal town - but even though those two are fairly obvious, no one even bats an eye. Maya heals animals super fast, talks with cougars like it's no big deal, and has visions of running through the forest - but that's what everyone has, right? Everyone can do that?<br /><br />The town was built by the totally-not suspicious St. Clouds and has a set-up straight out of a Stephen King horror novel - but again, totes legit.<br /><br />Maya's friend, Serena, died "drowning" the previous year in a lake that should be called a kiddie pool, but even though Serena was a top notch swimmer, no one bats an eye. Maya has a friend Daniel, who is totally not into her in the romantic way. Nope nope, that would be weird.<br /><br />And the new "bad boy", Rafe, is totally hot and sexy in that Latino way, so that means it's totally okay to break your rule about dating local boys for a makeout session or seventeen - RIGHT??!<br /><br />All the problems of this book go back to One Ultimate Problem: there is too little story spread out over 359 pages. <br /><br />There is nothing inherently wrong with Maya's character (I love how she's Native with Native culture) or Daniel or Rafe or the setup of the town or the mysterious death of Serena. Actually, all this could be a setup to a great horror movie! (Okay, maybe not great, but scary, definitely.)<br /><br />The problem is, this book is basically the first two chapters or so of a real book. It's all setup, not even a teensie bit of a payout.<br /><br />Do we find out how Serena died? Nope.<br /><br />Do we find out how Mina died? Nope.<br /><br />Do we find out how the fire was set? Nope. (Bonus: How were the kids SO SURE that the fire was set?)<br /><br />Do we know anything about Maya's family? Nope.<br /><br />Do we get confirmation about Rafe's assertions or do we just believe him because he's HAWT? Hot, duh!<br /><br />And on. And on. And so forth.<br /><br />It doesn't help that so much of the book feels like the same basic plot as Darkest Powers - girl finds out (from someone else who infodumps it to her, because GOD FORBID a woman know her own magical powers without being told by a male!) she's something special, super-evil medical corporation wants to use kid(s) for EVUL. Perhaps if we hadn't already read this plot in Darkest Powers, we could put up with Maya slamming her tongue down Rafe's throat for 200+ pages, but come on, Armstrong. We aren't idiots. Your characters aren't idiots. Open their eyes and let them see what's standing right in front of them.<br /><br />Oh and some of the survival tactics run completely counter to everything I'd read before. Pepper spray? Actually, <a href="http://bestpepperspray.net/pepper-spray-legal-canada/" rel="nofollow noopener">it is ILLEGAL to have in Canada</a>, though it will allow bear and dog spray - neither of which are mentioned in the book. Most <a href="http://www.safebee.com/outdoors/what-do-if-you-encounter-mountain-lion" rel="nofollow noopener"> sites say not to run away if you meet a cougar. And probably the biggest one is about </a><a href="http://www.bearsmart.com/about-bears/dispelling-myths/" rel="nofollow noopener">climbing a tree to escape a bear</a>. Armstrong, I hate to be rude, but did you do research or just make some of this up for drama?<br /><br />Common sense tells me I should avoid the sequel based on my dislike of this book; however, I am hopeful, with 359 pages of setup out of the way, perhaps we can get to the actual story. Plus I own all three books.<br /><br />(On a side note...I used to snap up all of Armstrong's books when they came out. Glad I'm not doing that anymore.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6561810041278065874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/582586546" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/582586546?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=on-the-run">on-the-run</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582586546" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18267042638515706986">The last 1/4 of the book...I don't even know where to start.<br/><br/>I don't know about you, but I'm not too fond of writing essays, and I was pretty terrible at it in grade school. I tend to BS my way through them then, I just ramble and make random, dramatic statements and reactions and not much actual facts until the very last part of my paper, where I realize, OH SHIT, I only have 250 words left, and I need to make a point!!!!!! Then I cram in all the facts I can and hope that my essay/paper ends up </span>
  <span id="freeText18267042638515706986" style="display:none">The last 1/4 of the book...I don't even know where to start.<br /><br />I don't know about you, but I'm not too fond of writing essays, and I was pretty terrible at it in grade school. I tend to BS my way through them then, I just ramble and make random, dramatic statements and reactions and not much actual facts until the very last part of my paper, where I realize, OH SHIT, I only have 250 words left, and I need to make a point!!!!!! Then I cram in all the facts I can and hope that my essay/paper ends up somewhat coherent. This is what it feels like Ms. Armstrong did for the ending. She fleshed out the first 3/4 of the book because she didn't have an idea of where she wants to go, then the hastily-thrown-together-before-deadline ending makes no sense.<br /><br />I'm sorry, is there an actual plot to this book? Ok, it's the first book in the series, and there needs to be introductions made, but I swear the first 2/3rds of the book was an introduction to Maya, her family, and her adopted past, her friend Serena's tragic accident, her mixed feelings and friendship with Daniel, and her burgeoning romance with the school poseu---I mean Rafe. Too much background. Way, way too much background, and not enough flesh or plot. I know more than I need to about how wonderful her parents are, the mean-spiritedness of bad-girl Sam, and the wonderful, pretty, scenic little town (and I mean little) owned by the St. Cloud corporation and all the hush-hush that goes on surrounding the lab. 75% through the book and I still had no idea what the plot is supposed to be.<br /><br />We hear the word "skinwalker" like twice in the first half. One by a crazy lazy who pretty much spitefully shouts it at Maya while she's about to get a tattoo. I really have no idea what this series wants to be. </span>

<div id="review_164384043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164384043" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164384043?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164384043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9116992839716367709">Here’s the thing that you need to know before you pick this up: it has no resolution. It’s three hundred and fifty nine pages of introduction. A wild and eerie setting is described, a cast of powerful teenagers is introduced, a few mysteries are presented, and a romance begins. And then it just ends. There isn’t even a real cliffhanger. However, I have to say that the elements that are present – the setting, the characters, the conflicts, and the romance – are all pretty well done. I don’t know </span>
  <span id="freeText9116992839716367709" style="display:none">Here’s the thing that you need to know before you pick this up: it has no resolution. It’s three hundred and fifty nine pages of introduction. A wild and eerie setting is described, a cast of powerful teenagers is introduced, a few mysteries are presented, and a romance begins. And then it just ends. There isn’t even a real cliffhanger. However, I have to say that the elements that are present – the setting, the characters, the conflicts, and the romance – are all pretty well done. I don’t know if it’s because I am still smarting a bit from the “ending” of The Darkest Powers trilogy, but the lack of any kind of resolution in this book really bothers me. Honestly, my recommendation is to wait for the second and third books of this series to be released before reading this one. You’ll probably save yourself a lot of frustration.<br /><br />This book takes place in a very remote part of Vancouver Island, in a tiny town called Salmon Creek. The terrain is lush and uncultivated, and inhabited by dangerous wildlife. Maya is a teenage girl who has been raised in Salmon Creek, which barely has a population of two hundred. All of the adults are employed by the St. Cloud corporation, a large medical research facility. I think that if you’ve read The Darkest Powers trilogy, you’ll have an immediate awareness that something’s not quite right in this town. Maya’s point of view, as a lifelong resident, is unsettling at times, but in a deliciously eerie way. It’s fascinating to experience how she views the St. Cloud corporation, almost like a benevolent trustworthy entity that she needs to defend.<br /><br />When Maya’s best friend Serena dies under mysterious circumstances, Maya vows to figure out what happened. But a year later, she’s still grieving, and avoiding any mention of Serena in an attempt to spare the feelings of her best friend Daniel, who was Serena’s boyfriend. When a journalist shows up in the town asking questions, and Maya starts having more cougar run-ins than can be considered healthy, she finally decides to get to the bottom of everything. Complicating her life is an attraction to the new kid in town, Rafe. Maya can tell that Rafe is never quite sincere about anything, and he seems to be a serial flirter, but she’s drawn to him anyway.<br /><br />Here is my biggest problem with this book: at my count, there are fifteen conflicts/mysteries that are set up in the course of these pages, and not a single one of them is solved. Not even the minor ones! Here’s the list that I came up with if you’re interested: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />1)	What’s the real motivation of the St. Cloud corporation? <br />2)	What’s going on with Rafe’s sister? <br />3)	Who drugged Maya at her birthday? <br />4)	Is Serena still alive? (And does anyone else think that she’s a siren?) <br />5)	What was the thing that grabbed her in the lake? <br />6)	Is Maya going to tell her parents about her powers? When will she shift? <br />7)	Where is her mother/brother? <br />8)	What are the powers of all of the other kids in Salmon Creek? <br />9)	Will Rafe outrun the drug dealers? <br />10)	 Who were the men in the woods? <br />11)	Why were they trying to round up the Salmon Creek kids? <br />12)	Who killed Mina Lee? <br />13)	 What relevance do Maya’s “animal memory vision” powers have? <br />14)	Will Daniel ever find out where his mother went?<br />15)	Will Rafe and Maya get together? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I found the last ¼ of this book to be simply exasperating. There’s useless filler thrown in (like Maya and Daniel’s detailed infiltration of the town hall meeting, where they jimmy open a window, find the perfect spot to listen in, hear a bunch of mundane details, find out <i>absolutely nothing</i> of importance, and then just leave), and the ending “chase” scenes seem packed with elements that I think are supposed to be thrilling but instead seem artificial and stupid. When Rafe and Maya get treed by a bear in one of the final scenes it just seems like, really? Aaaaallll of the potential conflicts that she could have spent time on, and we have to deal with BEAR ATTACKS?! How about resolving even one or two of the more minor mysteries?<br /><br />So yes, the huge gaping lack of resolution in this story really bothers me. But, I still love the characters (Daniel in particular), the fantastic setting, and I like the romance for the most part. The relationship between Maya and Rafe is mature and sweet. I will probably read the second book in this trilogy…but I may wait for the third book to be released before I do!<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Bjork – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sb8xgoeDojE&amp;feature=related" rel="nofollow noopener">Frosti</a><br /><br />Yeah, it’s haunting and strange and beautiful. It’s also only a minute and a half long with no words…and all it makes me want to do is move on to the next song (Aurora) which it leads in to.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9116992839716367709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_180525530" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180525530" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180525530?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062103529" href="/book/show/11318028-the-gathering">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=paranormal-ya">paranormal-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180525530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9762428078845167410">My history with Kelley Armstrong is a long and solid one.<br/>I've read all her books in the Underworld series and Elena and Clay are one of my (few) most beloved couples in UF. <br/>I inhaled all the books where they are protagonists, they're definitely my favorite in the series.<br/><br/>When Armstrong started writing YA lit (The Darkest Powers series) I picked up <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2800905.The_Summoning__Darkest_Powers___1_' title='The Summoning (Darkest Powers, #1) by Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Summoning</a>. I wasn't very impressed, so much so that I dropped the series. <br/>This new series, Darkness Rising, is somewhat better than DP, but still h</span>
  <span id="freeText9762428078845167410" style="display:none">My history with Kelley Armstrong is a long and solid one.<br />I've read all her books in the Underworld series and Elena and Clay are one of my (few) most beloved couples in UF. <br />I inhaled all the books where they are protagonists, they're definitely my favorite in the series.<br /><br />When Armstrong started writing YA lit (The Darkest Powers series) I picked up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2800905.The_Summoning__Darkest_Powers___1_" title="The Summoning (Darkest Powers, #1) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">The Summoning</a>. I wasn't very impressed, so much so that I dropped the series. <br />This new series, Darkness Rising, is somewhat better than DP, but still hasn't left me very impressed so far. <br /><br />The story is set in a tiny community somewhere on Vancouver Island, Canada. Salmon Creek is a small village whose residents work for a pharmaceutical company who does classified medical research. There's something definitely fishy going on in the community: from Serena's - Maya's best friend - death, to the appearance of an ever- increasing number of unknown cougars, to a series of weird events punctuating Maya's life. <br /><br />There were some nice - and original - aspects to this story that I particularly appreciated. <br />The setting, for starters, is really nice. Descriptions of the community, the wilderness and the wildlife are really well done, atmospheric. There's always an animalistic taste to Armstrong's books when she deals with shapeshifters that I find extremely enticing. <br />Because after all, shapeshifters they are, in this book. Skin-walkers, to be precise, a race of supernaturals that I had yet to encounter in fantasy. <br /><br />The mythology, tied to native Americans, is definitely a point which I found very interesting and that I would have wanted to - and that I hope will be - explored more in the next installments. What I didn't like was when said mythology got contaminated with a not-so-native regional Italian secret sect of hunters, the Benandanti, which had, in my opinion, very little to do with native Americans. There might be ignorance on my part on this subject but the sect is, incidentally, originally from the area where I live and I am pretty sure we have nothing in common with native American shapeshifters. Anyway. <br /><br />The other problem I had is that some scenes between Maya and Rafe, especially the ones when they are in the woods, felt very much similar to some Elena and Clay's scenes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and if they're similar now, I can't imagine how similar they will be when they will play in the forest as cougars  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />So basically, while I enjoyed the book (cliffhanger aside) I had the distinct feeling that this - or part of this - was just a YA version of a story that's already been successfully told. <br />I wish Kelley Armstrong had just stuck to adult urban fantasy because, to me, it definitely feels like she's trying to milk the YA cash cow by exploiting some trite paranormal YA tropes.<br /><br />For this review and more follow <a href="http://thenocturnallibrary.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nocturnal Library</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9762428078845167410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_102352057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102352057" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102352057?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102352057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8136590643856479083">3.5 stars<br/><br/>I really liked Armstrong's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8269450.Darkest_Powers_Trilogy__Darkest_Powers___1_3_' title='Darkest Powers Trilogy (Darkest Powers, #1-3) by Kelley Armstrong' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkest Powers Trilogy: The Reckoning, the Summoning, the Awakening</a>, so I was excited that this trilogy is set in that same world with a different set of kids. <br/><br/><b>The Things I loved:</b><br/><br/>1) I <i>loved</i> that, unlike every other YA out there, Maya had a great relationship with her parents. Yes, she was adopted, so there could be potentially creepy birth-parents lurking out there, but I'm a firm believer that the people who raise you are your <i>real</i> parents. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I'm</span></span>
  <span id="freeText8136590643856479083" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />I really liked Armstrong's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8269450.Darkest_Powers_Trilogy__Darkest_Powers___1_3_" title="Darkest Powers Trilogy (Darkest Powers, #1-3) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkest Powers Trilogy: The Reckoning, the Summoning, the Awakening</a>, so I was excited that this trilogy is set in that same world with a different set of kids. <br /><br /><b>The Things I loved:</b><br /><br />1) I <i>loved</i> that, unlike every other YA out there, Maya had a great relationship with her parents. Yes, she was adopted, so there could be potentially creepy birth-parents lurking out there, but I'm a firm believer that the people who raise you are your <i>real</i> parents. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm assuming that the nasty guy at the end with the gun was her birth-father, but it sounds like her birth-mother could have just given her up to keep her safe. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> At any rate, the dysfunctional parent thing is wearing a little thin, so this was a nice change.<br /><br />2) Armstrong is a great storyteller. This book could have been really boring...and it wasn't. I scarfed it down in one day if that tells you anything. The opening chapter really grabbed me, mostly because I didn't see it coming. Nice.<br /><br />3) Daniel. Loved him. <br /><br />And that leads me to...<br /><br /><b>Things I Didn't Love</b><br /><br />1) Rafe. Oh, I <i>liked</i> him, I just didn't like him <i>that</i> way. He was just so...blah. I'm really hoping that Armstrong pulls a switcheroo, and Maya ends up with Daniel. Not getting my hopes up though, since Armstrong seemed to be trying awful hard to make him seem like a misunderstood bad-boy with a heart of gold.<br /><br />2) <i>Not much happened in this story.</i> Well, stuff happened, but I kept waiting for it to really get cranking, and...eh. It felt like I was waiting on these kids to figure out what I knew from the first page. <i>Hurry up and get it already!</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Honestly, I didn't feel like they had a very good grasp of the situation by the end of the book. I didn't even feel any real urgency to <i>discover the truth</i> as they were getting on the helicopter. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I would almost recommend staying away from the previous books in this world because you have too much information to plod along with these guys if you do.<br /><br />3) One of the least exciting cliffhangers (if that's what it was supposed to be) I've ever read. Don't get me wrong, I want to read the rest of the books, because I'm guessing that this is just a really slow set-up, but I was hoping for some kind of exciting climax at the end. Or <i>something</i>. <br /><br />At the end of the day, though, Armstrong's writing still wins out. I'm hooked. I might as well go ahead and put the next book on my to-read list right now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8136590643856479083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98135413" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98135413?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=library-finds">library-finds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98135413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1028577664097190305"><br/><br/>First thoughts when I found this book in the library: “Yes! Score!” Full disclosure: Kelley Armstrong is one of my favorite Canadian authors. I love her easy-going storytelling style. I was a bit hesitant to pick up this book because I did not enjoy her Darkest Powers series as much as her adult series.<br/><br/>I was pleasantly surprised by this book. I was captivated by the story and could not put the book down. <i>The Gathering</i> is the story of Maya Delaney, a 16 year old girl who lives in an extremely iso</span>
  <span id="freeText1028577664097190305" style="display:none"><br /><br />First thoughts when I found this book in the library: “Yes! Score!” Full disclosure: Kelley Armstrong is one of my favorite Canadian authors. I love her easy-going storytelling style. I was a bit hesitant to pick up this book because I did not enjoy her Darkest Powers series as much as her adult series.<br /><br />I was pleasantly surprised by this book. I was captivated by the story and could not put the book down. <i>The Gathering</i> is the story of Maya Delaney, a 16 year old girl who lives in an extremely isolated community on Vancouver Island. Salmon Creek is home to about 200 residents who all work in mysterious research jobs for the St. Cloud Corporation. The residents have excellent health care, fantastic school, and good housing. That’s about all the information you get on the St. Cloud Corporation.<br /><br />The setting was truly a win. Every time that I travel to British Columbia, it never ceases to amaze me just how isolated you can be only a few miles from a city or town. For some pictures of the area click <a href="http://www.darkestpowers.com/maya-surveillance.php" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />I really liked Maya’s character. She is strong and stands up for herself. She keeps her wits about her and doesn’t risk everything to get the boy. Definitely not a doormat! I love how the author slowly builds up Maya’s abilities. The reader learns about Maya’s powers at the same time as Maya. Maya’s affinity with animals was cute. Fitz the three legged bobcat, Marv the cougar, even her dog Kenji, all were attracted to Maya. <br /><br />The other teenage characters were interesting as well. I can’t wait to see what becomes of Daniel. Rafe, the resident bad boy, seems to have a lot of surprises and secrets.<br /><br />The inclusion of the cabals from Armstrong’s adult series was genius. As her YA readers get older, they will enjoy the connection of this series to Armstrong’s Men and Women of the Otherworld series. <br /><br />My notes at the end of the book simply said: “ARGH! Don’t end the book here! I have so many questions! I want more! 2012 is too far away.”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1028577664097190305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_130907303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130907303" />
    <a title="Beth Dawkins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2604779-beth-dawkins"><img alt="Beth Dawkins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377023416p2/2604779.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130907303?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Dawkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Dawkins" href="/user/show/2604779-beth-dawkins">Beth Dawkins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130907303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12467903752603848306">Maya lives in a small research town. She is recovering after her best friend's questionable death. When she starts to look into it with Daniel, boyfriend of her dead friend. Instead of discovering answers all they find are more questions about themselves, and the town. <br/><br/>Sometimes I feel jealous of YA novels. The covers are so pretty and there are so many. I wonder if there were so many when I was in school. I don't remember, but I think the Urban Fantasy craze picked up before I graduated. So whe</span>
  <span id="freeText12467903752603848306" style="display:none">Maya lives in a small research town. She is recovering after her best friend's questionable death. When she starts to look into it with Daniel, boyfriend of her dead friend. Instead of discovering answers all they find are more questions about themselves, and the town. <br /><br />Sometimes I feel jealous of YA novels. The covers are so pretty and there are so many. I wonder if there were so many when I was in school. I don't remember, but I think the Urban Fantasy craze picked up before I graduated. So when I read a YA novel I always ask myself, 'am I jealous?' The answer for this one is yes. <br /><br />It is fast paced, easy to read (but also a beta run right now so it could change.)and has a action packed story. This is also the first thing I have ever read by Kelly Armstrong, but I look forward to reading more from her in the near future. She does an amazing job with bringing the characters through with dialogue which made it special. I want to read the next one, now, but that won't be for a while since this one is not even out yet. <br /><br />Then why a four, and not five stars? Two reasons, there are books we read for entertainment, and books we read for its depth. This is entertainment. The magical five star books are those that can weave both and bring us face to face with the characters. This is not one of those. The second reason is a lack of.. well more. Its a YA novel so the description is not grand because we don't want to bore our teens to death. I don't know if I fully believe that lack of description is a good thing. Then again I have always been a 'push the limits' girl.<br /><br />Bottom line is that I do think this story has promise and I look forward to another one... It left me wanting more. Which, lucky me, the author has LOTS more to gobble up. I don't think it is for everyone but I would have liked it as a young teen (12?). Its also a book that a mother and daughter could share and discuss.<br /><br />There is a fair amount of supernatural in the book. All of the main characters start to show some type of ability. This amounted to tense situations. It does have a fair amount of romance, but nothing, in my opinion, that is too racy for teens. It tries to work in a love triangle between Maya, Daniel and bad boy Rafe. Still the romance feels like background noise in comparison to the action and danger surrounding the teens.<br /><br />All this is just a impression, I didn't go into details about the story because it is a beta, a lot could change. I did enjoy it! After a cliff hanger ending, I am ready for the second. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12467903752603848306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
